                     <orth lang="ar">طَوڤفَ</orth>
                  </form> The inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">طَوَافٌ</foreign> primarily signifies, accord. to Er-Rághib, The act of <hi rend="ital">going,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">walking,</hi> in an absolute sense: or the <hi rend="ital">going,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">walking, around,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">otherwise.</hi> (MF, TA.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">طَافَ حَوْلَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّىْءِ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign>, (Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">حَوْلَ الكَعْبَةِ</foreign>, (O, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">بِهَا</foreign>, (K,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَطُوفُ</foreign>, (S, O, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">طَوْفٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">طَوَافٌ</foreign> (O, Msb, K, and mentioned also in the S but not there said to be an inf. n.) and <foreign lang="ar">طَوَفَانٌ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) [and perhaps <foreign lang="ar">طُوفَانٌ</foreign>, q. v.,] <hi rend="ital">He went round</hi> or <hi rend="ital">round about, circuited,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">circuited around,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">compassed,</hi> (Msb, TA,) <hi rend="ital">the thing,</hi> (S, Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">the Kaabeh;</hi> (O, K;) and so <foreign lang="ar">طَافَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَطِيفُ</foreign>; (Msb; [but this I think doubtful;]) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27309-0-1" target="تطوّف" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27310"/></foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) and

(TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">طُفْتُ بِهِ عَلَى البَيْتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I went round the House</hi> of God, i. e. the Kaabeh, <hi rend="ital">with him;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">I made him to go round,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to circuit,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">compass, the House.</hi> (Msb.                      <orth lang="ar">أَطْوَفَ</orth>
                  </form> see 1, in two places.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">اطاف بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign> signifies also <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, surrounded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">encompassed, the thing.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">اطاف بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He came to him; visited him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">alighted at his abode as a guest;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَلَمَّ بِهِ</foreign>: and <hi rend="ital">he approached him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">drew,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, near to him;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">قَارَبَهُ</foreign>. (S, K.) [And] <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27309-2-1" target="طَافَ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِالنِّسَآءِ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَطُوفُ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">اطاف</foreign>; <hi rend="ital">He came to women,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the women; visited them;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">alighted at their abodes as a guest;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَلَمَّ</foreign> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">اطاف بِهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He came to him by night:</hi> and sometimes improperly used as meaning by day: a poet says, <pb n="1893"/>
